Repetitive and low complexity regions of the scaffolds were masked using RepeatMasker<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="RepeatMasker Open-3.0 v.http://www.repeatmasker.org (1996–2010)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1761">36</a></sup> based on self-alignments and homology with the RepBase public database and specific databases built with RepeatModeler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="RepeatModeler Open-1.0 v.http://www.repeatmasker.org (2008–2010)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1765">37</a></sup>. LTR retrotransposons were detected by LTRharvest<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Ellinghaus, D., Kurtz, S. &amp; Willhoeft, U. LTRharvest, an efficient and flexible software for de novo detection of LTR retrotransposons. BMC Bioinformatics 9, 18 (2008)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1769">38</a></sup>. Repeat elements were classified with TEclass<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Abrusán, G., Grundmann, N., DeMester, L. &amp; Makalowski, W. TEclass—a tool for automated classification of unknown eukaryotic transposable elements. Bioinformatics 25, 1329–1330 (2009)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1773">39</a></sup> and RepeatClassifier<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="RepeatModeler Open-1.0 v.http://www.repeatmasker.org (2008–2010)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1778">37</a></sup>. The 5′ and 3′ ends of each LTR identified by LTRharvest were aligned with MUSCLE and used to calculate the nucleotide divergence rate with the Kimura-2 parameter using MEGA5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Tamura, K. et al. MEGA5: Molecular Evolutionary Genetics Analysis Using Maximum Likelihood, Evolutionary Distance and Maximum Parsimony Methods. Mol. Biol. Evol. 28, 2731–2739 (2011)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1782">40</a></sup>. The insertion time was estimated by assuming an average substitution rate of 1.3 × 10e-8, as in the common bean<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Schmutz, J. et al. A reference genome for common bean and genome-wide analysis of dual domestications. Nat. Genet. 46, 707–713 (2014)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1786">5</a></sup> analysis.</p><p><i>De novo</i> and genome guided <i>ab initio</i> transcripts were assembled from RNA-Seq reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Yates, S. et al. De novo assembly of red clover transcriptome based on RNA-Seq data provides insight into drought response, gene discovery and marker identification. BMC Genomics 15, 453 (2014)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1798">10</a></sup> using Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotech. 29, 644–652 (2011)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1802">41</a></sup> and Tophat/Cufflinks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nat. Protocols 7, 562–578 (2012)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1806">42</a></sup>, respectively. Additionally, exon-intron junctions were deduced from the mapping positions of the reads. Junctions supported by more than 3 reads were incorporated as evidence in Augustus. Assembled transcripts were aligned to the assembly and clustered in novel transcript models using PASA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 5654–5666 (2003)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1810">43</a></sup>. A high quality full-length non-redundant subset from the <i>ab initio</i> transcript models from PASA was used as a training set for Augustus. The proteins of the Fabaceae family in Uniprot and TrEMBL and the transcripts annotated in the soybean, common bean and <i>M. truncatula</i> genomes were aligned to the masked genome using Exonerate<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Slater, G. &amp; Birney, E. Automated generation of heuristics for biological sequence comparison. BMC Bioinformatics 6, 31 (2005)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1821">44</a></sup>.</p><p>Gene models were predicted by GeneID<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Guigo, R., Knudsen, S., Drake, N. &amp; Smith, T. F. Prediction of gene structure. J. Mol. Biol. 226, 141–157 (1992)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1828">45</a></sup> and SNAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 59 (2004)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1832">46</a></sup> in the masked version of the assembly and by Augustus in the unmasked version of the assembly. Augustus builds the gene models to be compatible with the information from the alignments, the transcript models and junctions deduced from the RNA-Seq data and annotated repeated regions and transposons. Additionally, alternative transcript models of a gene were reported for those incompatible with the provided alignments and transcript information.</p><p>Finally, RNA-Seq reads were mapped again using the guidance of the generated annotation by Tophat, a new set of transcripts assembled by Cufflinks and alternative splicing incorporated in the annotation by PASA. The annotated features were stored in an EnsEMBL database to allow visualisation and exportation.</p><p>The functional annotation of the proteome was done with an in-house pipeline (AnnotF) that compares the results of Blast2GO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674–3676 (2005)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1842">47</a></sup> and InterProSCAN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236–1240 (2014)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1846">48</a></sup>. Clustering was based on eggNOG clusters. Genes within pathways were compared with RAxML 8.0.22<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312–1313, (2014)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1850">49</a></sup> (100 bootstrap replications). The proteomes of four Fabaceae species and <i>A. thaliana</i> were aligned and single gene clusters filtered and concatenated after removing gaps using HAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Robbertse, B., Yoder, R. J., Boyd, A., Reeves, J. &amp; Spatafora, J. W. Hal: an Automated Pipeline for Phylogenetic Analyses of Genomic Data. PLoS Currents 3, RRN1213 (2011)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1857">50</a></sup>. A phylogenetic tree based on these data was built with MEGA6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Tamura, K., Stecher, G., Peterson, D., Filipski, A. &amp; Kumar, S. MEGA6: Molecular Evolutionary Genetics Analysis Version 6.0. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 2725–2729 (2013)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1862">51</a></sup> using Maximum-likelihood and 100 bootstrap replications. Divergence times in the phylogenetic tree were calculated with the RelTime method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Tamura, K. et al. Estimating divergence times in large molecular phylogenies. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 109, 19333–19338 (2012)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1866">52</a></sup> in MEGA6 using the divergence date between common bean and soybean as reference<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Schmutz, J. et al. Genome sequence of the palaeopolyploid soybean. Nature 463, 178–183 (2010)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1870">6</a></sup>. The gene density was calculated by dividing the total number of genes by the total length of each genome. Additionally, we calculated the same value for each interval of 10 Kb along the genome. The distribution of these values is reported as “mean number of genes in 10 Kb intervals”.</p><p>Syntenic blocks were identified with MUMMER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1877">53</a></sup>, analysed with SyMap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Soderlund, C., Nelson, W., Shoemaker, A. &amp; Paterson, A. SyMAP: A system for discovering and viewing syntenic regions of FPC maps. Genome Res. 16, 1159–1168 (2006)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1881">54</a></sup>, using the default parameters, but with the requirement of 30 gene pairs to call a syntenic block and plotted with Circos<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Krzywinski, M. et al. Circos: An information aesthetic for comparative genomics. Genome Res. 19, 1639–1645 (2009)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1885">55</a></sup>. The syntenic gene pairs were aligned with MAFFT v 7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT Multiple Sequence Alignment Software Version 7: Improvements in Performance and Usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1889">56</a></sup> and the alignments used to calculate the Kimura rates with MEGA6 in order to estimate the nucleotide divergence rates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Linkage disequilibrium</h3><p>A population consisting of 86 genotypes from the red clover variety Lea (Graminor, Norway) was sown as part of a field experiment in Southern Norway. Genotyping by sequencing methodology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Elshire, R. J. et al. A Robust, Simple Genotyping-by-Sequencing (GBS) Approach for High Diversity Species. PLoS ONE 6, e19379 (2011)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1901">57</a></sup> was used to obtain SNP polymorphisms in the population. A minimum of 10 reads for each individual and in the case of heterozygotes, a minimum of 2 reads of the minor allele, were required for SNP calling. After removing SNPs with missingness &gt;0.20, or minor allele frequency &lt;0.05, a total of 3942 SNPs were identified, of which 2161 were mapped onto the 7 pseudomolecules. LD heatmaps and associated plots were produced using R<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="R. Core Team (2013). R: A language and environment for statistical computing. R Foundation for Statistical Computing, Vienna, Austria. URL &#xA;                    http://www.R-project.org/&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1905">58</a></sup> as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Wang, L., Sorensen, P., Janss, L., Ostersen, T. &amp; Edwards, D. Genome-wide and local pattern of linkage disequilibrium and persistence of phase for 3 Danish pig breeds. BMC Genet. 14, 115 (2013)." href="/articles/srep17394#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d30673e1909">59</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec16" data-title="Additional Information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec16-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec16">Additional Information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec16-content"><p><b>Accession codes:</b> All shotgun read libraries (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/srep17394#MOESM1">Supplementary Table 5</a>) and the assembly are deposited in the European Nucleotide Archive (accession PRJEB9186).</p><p><b>Data Availability</b>: The genome assembly and annotation can also be downloaded as individual files (<a href="https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.17232">http://dx.doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.17232</a>) or browsed online (<a href="http://tgac-browser.tgac.ac.uk/trifolium_pratense">http://tgac-browser.tgac.ac.uk/trifolium_pratense</a>). Accession numbers of the BAC end sequences are HR235466-298279.</p><p><b>How to cite this article</b>: De Vega, J. J. <i>et al.</i> Red clover (<i>Trifolium pratense</i> L.) draft genome provides a platform for trait improvement. <i>Sci. Rep.</i> <b>5</b>, 17394; doi: 10.1038/srep17394 (2015).</p></div></div></section>
